	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" >Sergio Agüero</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sergio_Aguero&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergio Aguero">Sergio Aguero</a>)</span></div>

		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Argentine association football player</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">In this <a href="/wiki/Spanish_name" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish name">Spanish name</a>, the first or paternal&#32;<a href="/wiki/Surname" title="Surname">surname</a> is <i> Agüero</i>&#32;and the second or maternal family name is <i> del Castillo</i>.</div>

* Senior club appearances and goals counted for the domestic league only&#32;and correct as of 22:04, 13 March 2021 (UTC)<br />‡ National team caps and goals correct as of 18 November 2019</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Sergio Leonel Agüero del Castillo</b> (<small>Spanish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[sexjo le.onel aweo]</a></span>; born 2 June 1988), colloquially known as <b>Kun Agüero</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> is an Argentine professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Striker" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentine national team</a>. He wears "Kun" on his shirt, a childhood nickname based on the title character from the cartoon <a href="/wiki/Kum-Kum" title="Kum-Kum">Kum-Kum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> He is widely considered as one of the best strikers of his generation and one of the best players in Premier League history.
</p><p>Agüero began his career at the Argentine <a href="/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Independiente" title="Club Atlético Independiente">Independiente</a>. On 5 July 2003, he became the youngest player to play in the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Primera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Argentine Primera División">Argentine Primera División</a> on his debut at 15 years and 35 days, breaking the record previously established by <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">Diego Maradona</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seasons_in_Argentine_football" class="mw-redirect" title="Seasons in Argentine football">1976</a>. In 2006, he moved to <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> side <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a>, for a transfer fee of €23 million. During his years at Madrid, he established himself as one of the best young players in Europe and won the <a href="/wiki/Don_Bal%C3%B3n_Award" title="Don Balón Award">Don Balón Award</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuttosport" title="Tuttosport">Tuttosport</a> <a href="/wiki/Golden_Boy_(award)" title="Golden Boy (award)">Golden Boy</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Soccer_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="World Soccer Awards">World Soccer Young Player of the Year</a>. He scored 101 goals in 234 appearances for Atlético, while winning the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Super_Cup" title="UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a>.
</p><p>Agüero moved to Premier League club Manchester City in July 2011 for an undisclosed fee in the region of £35 million. On the last day of his debut season with the club, he scored a 94th-minute winner against <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> that earned City its first league title in 44 years. In the 2014–15 season, he won the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a>. In November 2017, Agüero became <a href="/wiki/List_of_Manchester_City_F.C._records_and_statistics#All-time_top_goalscorers" title="List of Manchester City F.C. records and statistics">Manchester City's all-time highest goal-scorer</a>, scoring his 178th City goal against <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He was named to the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a> in <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year_(2010s)#Premier_League_9" title="PFA Team of the Year (2010s)">2017–18</a> and <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year_(2010s)#Premier_League_10" title="PFA Team of the Year (2010s)">2018–19</a>. He is currently the 4th highest goalscorer in Premier League history, and the highest non-English scorer in the history of the competition, with <a href="/wiki/List_of_footballers_with_100_or_more_Premier_League_goals" title="List of footballers with 100 or more Premier League goals">181 goals in the division</a>. He also holds the record for <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_hat-tricks" title="List of Premier League hat-tricks">most hat-tricks in the Premier League</a>, with twelve.
</p><p>At the international level, Agüero represented the <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_under-20_football_team" title="Argentina national under-20 football team">Argentina under-20 team</a> at the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="FIFA U-20 World Cup">FIFA U-20 World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="2005 FIFA World Youth Championship">2005</a> and in <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2007 FIFA U-20 World Cup">2007</a>, winning both tournaments.<sup id="cite_ref-rise2_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rise2-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He played at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2008 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s tournament">2008 Beijing Olympics</a>, scoring two goals in the 3–0 semi-final win against <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_under-23_football_team" title="Brazil national under-23 football team">Brazil</a> as Argentina went on to win the gold medal.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Agüero was selected to represent <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">the senior team</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2011_Copa_Am%C3%A9rica" title="2011 Copa América">2011 Copa América</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2015_Copa_Am%C3%A9rica" title="2015 Copa América">2015 Copa América</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Am%C3%A9rica_Centenario" title="Copa América Centenario">Copa América Centenario</a>, reaching the finals of the latter three tournaments. He also participated in the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>, where he scored his first and second World Cup goals for Argentina, and the <a href="/wiki/2019_Copa_Am%C3%A9rica" title="2019 Copa América">2019 Copa América</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independiente">Independiente</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aguero_Independiente_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Aguero_Independiente_2005.jpg/140px-Aguero_Independiente_2005.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="329" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Aguero_Independiente_2005.jpg/210px-Aguero_Independiente_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/36/Aguero_Independiente_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="248" data-file-height="583" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aguero_Independiente_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Agüero with Independiente in 2005</div></div></div>
<p>Sergio Agüero joined the youth system of <a href="/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Independiente" title="Club Atlético Independiente">Independiente</a> at the age of nine. He started playing for the side, becoming the youngest player to debut in the first division at 15 years and 35 days (on 5 July 2003 against <a href="/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_San_Lorenzo_de_Almagro" class="mw-redirect" title="Club Atlético San Lorenzo de Almagro">Club Atlético San Lorenzo de Almagro</a>), when Independiente's coach, <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Ruggeri" title="Oscar Ruggeri">Oscar Ruggeri</a> sent Agüero onto the field as a substitute for <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Benito_Rivas" class="mw-redirect" title="Emanuel Benito Rivas">Emanuel Rivas</a> in the 69th minute of the match.<sup id="cite_ref-rise_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rise-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> His performance was well received by the press.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Despite his early debut, he was not selected again by Ruggeri, and his replacement <a href="/wiki/Osvaldo_Sosa" title="Osvaldo Sosa">Osvaldo Sosa</a>, for the remainder of <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Argentine_Primera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="2002–03 Argentine Primera División">2002–03 season</a>, having made only one appearance in the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_in_Argentine_football" title="2002–03 in Argentine football">Torneo Clausura</a>. Following the arrival of coach <a href="/wiki/Jose_Omar_Pastoriza" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose Omar Pastoriza">Jose Omar Pastoriza</a>, seven months after Agüero's first match he returned to the club's first-team in 4–2 win against <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru's</a> <a href="/wiki/Cienciano" title="Cienciano">Cienciano</a> during the group stages of the <a href="/wiki/2004_Copa_Libertadores" title="2004 Copa Libertadores">2004 Copa Libertadores</a>. This meant that he also became the youngest player to participate in the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a>, a record that he held for three years.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> One month later, Agüero again featured in a Copa Libertadores fixture against <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador's</a> <a href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_El_Nacional" class="mw-redirect" title="Club Deportivo El Nacional">El Nacional</a>. On 19 June, for the first time, Agüero played a full 90-minute match for Independiente against <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_de_Rafaela" title="Atlético de Rafaela">Atlético de Rafaela</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Argentine_Primera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="2003–04 Argentine Primera División">Torneo Clausura</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for Independiente in a 2–2 draw against <a href="/wiki/Estudiantes_de_la_Plata" class="mw-redirect" title="Estudiantes de la Plata">Estudiantes</a> on 26 November, with a 22nd minute shot from outside the penalty area.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bio_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Agüero became a regular in the club's first-team, being selected for the <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_under-20_football_team" title="Argentina national under-20 football team">Argentina U-20 squad</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2005_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="2005 FIFA World Youth Championship">2005 FIFA U-20 World Cup</a>, which Argentina won.
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_in_Argentine_football" title="2005–06 in Argentine football">2005–06 season</a>, Agüero scored 18 goals in 36 league appearances, having missed two games due to suspension. In a 4–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Racing_Club_de_Avellaneda" title="Racing Club de Avellaneda">Racing</a> on 11 September, he dribbled from inside of his own half and scored Independiente's fourth goal with a left footed shot.<sup id="cite_ref-bio_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> His first red card came in the Torneo Apertura, after slapping an opponent in a match against <a href="/wiki/Tiro_Federal" title="Tiro Federal">Tiro Federal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> His outstanding performances during the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Argentine_Primera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="2005–06 Argentine Primera División">Torneo Apertura</a> attracted interest from a number of large European clubs, and, after months of speculation, Agüero announced on TV in April that he intended to leave the club at the end of the season. Before the end of the season, there had already been speculation of a possible transfer to <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bio_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> With his performances being lauded by the press, there was talk of a possible call up for Agüero for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In a 2–0 away victory against <a href="/wiki/Olimpo_de_Bahia_Blanca" class="mw-redirect" title="Olimpo de Bahia Blanca">Olimpo de Bahia Blanca</a> in round 17 of the Torneo Clausura, Agüero received his fifth yellow card of the season. This prevented him from playing his last game for Independiente in a fixture against <a href="/wiki/Boca_Juniors" title="Boca Juniors">Boca Juniors</a> in <a href="/wiki/Avellaneda" title="Avellaneda">Avellaneda</a> one week later. The yellow card brought tears to his eyes, as television cameras recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Agüero, who scored Independiente's second goal of the match later said "I think that it was my last goal for Independiente". He played his last game for Independiente, two weeks later, in a 2–0 away defeat to <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Central" title="Rosario Central">Rosario Central</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On 30 May, Agüero officially transferred to Atlético Madrid for €20 million, marking a record for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Atl.C3.A9tico_Madrid"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Atlético_Madrid">Atlético Madrid</span></h3>
<h4><span id="2006.E2.80.9307_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2006–07_season">2006–07 season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SergioAg%C3%BCero.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/SergioAg%C3%BCero.jpg/170px-SergioAg%C3%BCero.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="322" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0e/SergioAg%C3%BCero.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="221" data-file-height="419" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SergioAg%C3%BCero.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Agüero playing for <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> in October 2007.</div></div></div>
<p>In May 2006, Agüero joined Spanish club <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> for a fee reported to be around €20 million, breaking the club's previous transfer record.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> He caused controversy early in his Atlético career by using his hands to score the winning goal against <a href="/wiki/Recreativo_de_Huelva" title="Recreativo de Huelva">Recreativo de Huelva</a> on 14 October 2006, only his second goal for the club, with the first coming in a 4–1 away win against <a href="/wiki/Athletic_Bilbao" title="Athletic Bilbao">Athletic Bilbao</a> on 17 September.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He ended his first season in Madrid with seven goals in all competitions, eased into European football by manager <a href="/wiki/Javier_Aguirre" title="Javier Aguirre">Javier Aguirre</a>, who opted to bring him in and out of the line-up as Atlético finished seventh, enough to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Intertoto_Cup" title="UEFA Intertoto Cup">UEFA Intertoto Cup</a>.
</p>
<h4><span id="2007.E2.80.9308_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007–08_season">2007–08 season</span></h4>
<p>Following the departure of strike partner <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Torres" title="Fernando Torres">Fernando Torres</a> to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in the summer of 2007, Agüero secured his starting spot for the <i>Rojiblancos</i> and soon became arguably the team's most important player at the age of just 19. In the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_La_Liga" title="2007–08 La Liga">2007–08 season</a>, he finished third highest scorer in <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a>, behind <a href="/wiki/Daniel_G%C3%BCiza" class="mw-redirect" title="Daniel Güiza">Daniel Güiza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Fabiano" title="Luís Fabiano">Luís Fabiano</a>, with 19 goals, and was runner up in the <i><a href="/wiki/Trofeo_Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano" title="Trofeo Alfredo Di Stéfano">Trofeo Alfredo Di Stéfano</a></i> award.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Agüero won many plaudits for his <a href="/wiki/Man_of_the_match" class="mw-redirect" title="Man of the match">man of the match</a> display against <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> in March 2008, scoring twice, assisting a goal and winning a penalty for Atlético in a 4–2 win.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He also scored important goals against the likes of <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencia_CF" title="Valencia CF">Valencia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Villarreal_CF" title="Villarreal CF">Villarreal</a> to help Atlético finish fourth and qualify for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> for the first time in over ten years.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2008.E2.80.9309_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008–09_season">2008–09 season</span></h4>
<p>Agüero was once again a regular goalscorer for Atlético in the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_La_Liga" title="2008–09 La Liga">2008–09 season</a>, continuing to establish a lethal partnership with <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguayan</a> striker <a href="/wiki/Diego_Forl%C3%A1n" title="Diego Forlán">Diego Forlán</a>, also a former Independiente player. On 16 September, he scored his first Champions League goals in a 3–0 away win at <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV</a>, helping Atlético eventually reach the last 16 of the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In March 2009, the duo of Forlán and Agüero scored a <a href="/wiki/Brace_(sports)#In_other_fields" class="mw-redirect" title="Brace (sports)">brace</a> each in a 4–3 win over league leaders Barcelona, the latter scoring the winning goal in the final minutes of the match.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> With the help of more vital goals in a formidable end of the season run-in from his team, Agüero finished in the top ten contenders for the <a href="/wiki/Pichichi_Trophy" title="Pichichi Trophy">Pichichi Trophy</a>, which was won by his teammate Forlán.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Atlético finished fourth in the league, qualifying for the following season's <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2009–10 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>.
</p>
<h4><span id="2009.E2.80.9310_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2009–10_season">2009–10 season</span></h4>
<p>Despite not being as prolific in front of goal, Agüero had another good season in <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_La_Liga" title="2009–10 La Liga">2009–10</a>, and was praised for his influential performances as Atlético enjoyed their most successful season in over a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On 3 November 2009, he scored twice against <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> during a 2–2 draw in the Champions League at the <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Calder%C3%B3n_Stadium" title="Vicente Calderón Stadium">Vicente Calderón</a>. Atlético were knocked out of the competition, but went on to reach the final of the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2009–10 UEFA Europa League">2009–10 UEFA Europa League</a>, where Agüero assisted both goals in a 2–1 <a href="/wiki/Extra_time" class="mw-redirect" title="Extra time">extra time</a> win against English club <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> He also helped Atlético reach the final of the <a href="/wiki/Copa_del_Rey" title="Copa del Rey">Copa del Rey</a>, although this time they were not victorious, losing to Sevilla in the <a href="/wiki/Camp_Nou" title="Camp Nou">Camp Nou</a> on 19 May.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2010.E2.80.9311_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–11_season">2010–11 season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pepe_y_aguero.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Pepe_y_aguero.jpg/220px-Pepe_y_aguero.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Pepe_y_aguero.jpg/330px-Pepe_y_aguero.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Pepe_y_aguero.jpg/440px-Pepe_y_aguero.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="798" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pepe_y_aguero.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Agüero (pictured with <a href="/wiki/Pepe_(footballer,_born_1983)" title="Pepe (footballer, born 1983)">Pepe</a>) with Atlético Madrid during the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_La_Liga" title="2010–11 La Liga">2010–11 season</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>On 27 August 2010, Atlético Madrid captured the <a href="/wiki/2010_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2010 UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a> by beating favorites <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Internazionale</a> 2–0. Agüero provided the assist for <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Antonio_Reyes" title="José Antonio Reyes">José Antonio Reyes</a>' opening goal and then secured the win by scoring the second.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On 4 January 2011, Atlético Madrid confirmed via their official website that Agüero had signed a new contract with the club, keeping him at the Vicente Calderón until 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The following day, he was named as the new <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">vice-captain</a> of Atlético, along with strike partner Diego Forlán.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_La_Liga" title="2010–11 La Liga">2010–11 season</a> was arguably Agüero's most successful for Atlético, as he scored 20 league goals for the first time in his career. Between March and May 2011, he went on a run of seven consecutive goalscoring appearances, a feat that no other player in Europe could match during the season.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Agüero's final outing for Atlético came on 21 May against <a href="/wiki/RCD_Mallorca" title="RCD Mallorca">Mallorca</a>, a game in which he reached two <a href="/wiki/Milestone" title="Milestone">milestones</a>. In a 4–3 win, he scored his first career <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a>, the second goal being his 100th for the <i>Colchoneros</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Failure to celebrate any of the goals, however, led to speculation that he would be on his way out of the club.
</p><p>On 23 May 2011, Agüero announced on his official website that he wanted to move from Atlético and formally asked to be released from his contract.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Agüero later spoke to <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, where he stated that he would "not be returning to Atlético".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> On the same day that Agüero officially became a <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> player, Atlético hosted a <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Europa_League_qualifying_phase_and_play-off_round" title="2011–12 UEFA Europa League qualifying phase and play-off round">2011–12 Europa League qualifier</a> against <a href="/wiki/Str%C3%B8msgodset_IF" title="Strømsgodset IF">Strømsgodset IF</a>, where a group of Atlético fans brandished "Agüero, We Hope You Die" banners in a reaction to the striker's transfer to City at the Vicente Calderón on 28 July 2011, after he had previously stated his desire to see out his contract with the club just weeks before requesting a transfer.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Upon his departure, Atlético used the money from Agüero's sale to buy <a href="/wiki/Radamel_Falcao" title="Radamel Falcao">Radamel Falcao</a> as his replacement.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_City">Manchester City</span></h3>
<h4><span id="2011.E2.80.9312_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–12_season"><a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Manchester_City_F.C._season" title="2011–12 Manchester City F.C. season">2011–12 season</a></span></h4>
<p>On 28 July 2011, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> confirmed that Agüero had signed a five-year contract with the club. The fee was reported to be <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_association_football_transfers" title="List of most expensive association football transfers">in the region of £35 million</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> He was given the number 16 shirt for his first season at City and wears the shirt name <b>Kun Agüero</b>. He was an unused substitute in the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Super_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Super Cup">Dublin Super Cup</a> match against Internazionale and the <a href="/wiki/2011_FA_Community_Shield" title="2011 FA Community Shield">2011 FA Community Shield</a> against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> with manager <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Mancini" title="Roberto Mancini">Roberto Mancini</a> believing Agüero was not yet fit.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Agüero made his debut for City on 15 August 2011 in a 4–0 Premier League victory over <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>. Agüero came on as a substitute in the 59th minute, scoring his first goal for the club within nine minutes after a tap-in from a cross from full back <a href="/wiki/Micah_Richards" title="Micah Richards">Micah Richards</a>. He then turned provider with an assist after chipping over the oncoming goalkeeper before flicking the ball back into the penalty box and into the path of <a href="/wiki/David_Silva" title="David Silva">David Silva</a> to score. Agüero rounded off his debut by scoring again in injury time with a 30-yard strike. His 30-minute debut gained rave reviews among football journalists, with some suggesting it was one of the best in English football.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>City continued their strong start, winning 3–2 away at <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> with Agüero missing two chances in the penalty box.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On 28 August, Agüero scored his third league goal in Manchester City's 5–1 rout of <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> On his third start for the club, he scored his first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_hat-tricks" title="List of Premier League hat-tricks">Premier League hat-trick</a>, against <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> On 18 September, he scored twice at <a href="/wiki/Craven_Cottage" title="Craven Cottage">Craven Cottage</a> against <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a>, but City were held to a 2–2 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Having been substituted after just 28 minutes due to an injury during a 4–0 win against <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> on 1 October, Agüero returned to action in a <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2011–12 UEFA Champions League">2011–12 UEFA Champions League</a> group stage fixture, where he came on for <a href="/wiki/Nigel_de_Jong" title="Nigel de Jong">Nigel de Jong</a> on 62 minutes and scored a 93rd-minute winner in his side's 2–1 victory against Villarreal on 18 October.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On 23 October, Agüero took part in his first <a href="/wiki/Manchester_derby" title="Manchester derby">Manchester derby</a>, scoring in the 69th minute as he converted a Micah Richards pass across the face of goal. The match finished 6–1 to City.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> On 1 November, Agüero was shortlisted for the prestigious <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Ballon_d%27Or" title="FIFA Ballon d&#39;Or">FIFA Ballon d'Or</a>. On 19 November, he scored a penalty in a 3–1 win at home to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, ending Newcastle's unbeaten start to the season.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nasri_%26_Aguero_with_trophy.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Nasri_%26_Aguero_with_trophy.JPG/220px-Nasri_%26_Aguero_with_trophy.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Nasri_%26_Aguero_with_trophy.JPG/330px-Nasri_%26_Aguero_with_trophy.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Nasri_%26_Aguero_with_trophy.JPG/440px-Nasri_%26_Aguero_with_trophy.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1352" data-file-height="1050" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nasri_%26_Aguero_with_trophy.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Agüero (right) and <a href="/wiki/Samir_Nasri" title="Samir Nasri">Samir Nasri</a> parade the Premier League trophy, May 2012.</div></div></div>
<p>Agüero made his <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a> debut in the quarter final match against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Stadium" title="Emirates Stadium">Emirates Stadium</a>, scoring the only goal of the game in the 83rd minute from an <a href="/wiki/Adam_Johnson_(footballer)" title="Adam Johnson (footballer)">Adam Johnson</a> through-ball.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> His next goal came in a 5–1 home win against <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a>, opening the scoring in the 32nd minute, giving him his 13th goal of the season and maintaining the team's 100% league record at home.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> On 21 December, he scored a brace as City beat <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> 3–0 at home.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On 3 January 2012, he opened the scoring in a 3–0 win at home to Liverpool, beating <a href="/wiki/Pepe_Reina" title="Pepe Reina">Pepe Reina</a> with a low shot.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Agüero scored his 15th goal on 4 February, scoring a penalty against Fulham in a 3–0 win at a snow-covered <a href="/wiki/City_of_Manchester_Stadium" title="City of Manchester Stadium">City of Manchester Stadium</a>.
</p><p>During the first-leg of a Europa League round of 32 match against <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">Porto</a>, Agüero entered the field in the 78th minute for <a href="/wiki/Mario_Balotelli" title="Mario Balotelli">Mario Balotelli</a> and scored the match-winning goal, and his first <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a> goal for Manchester City, in the 85th minute.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The game ended 2–1, and, in the second-leg, Agüero scored within 19 seconds in a 4–0 win on 22 February. Manchester City advanced to the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Europa_League_knockout_phase#Round_of_16" title="2011–12 UEFA Europa League knockout phase">last 16</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2011–12 UEFA Europa League">2011–12 UEFA Europa League</a>, having won 6–1 on aggregate. On 25 February, Agüero scored his 16th league goal in a 3–0 win against Blackburn.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> During the second-leg of Manchester City's <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Europa_League_knockout_phase#Round_of_16" title="2011–12 UEFA Europa League knockout phase">Round of 16 Europa League</a> fixture against <a href="/wiki/Sporting_Clube_de_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Sporting Clube de Portugal">Sporting CP</a> on 15 March, Agüero netted a double to help City claim a 3–2 win, having been trailing 2–0 at half-time, to level the scores at 3–3 on aggregate. Sporting CP won on away goals, as they defeated Manchester City 1–0 in the first-leg on 8 March.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> One week later, Agüero scored his 17th league goal in 2–1 win against Chelsea on 21 March.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On 29 March, Agüero was ruled out for 10 days to two weeks due to a foot problem, which was later diagnosed as a reaction to a substance that blistered his foot.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 April, Agüero scored two goals for himself and also set up another two goals (for David Silva and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Tevez" title="Carlos Tevez">Carlos Tevez</a>) in a 4–0 home victory against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> On 14 April, Agüero scored a double in a 6–1 away win against Norwich City, his two goals meaning that he had surpassed 20 league goals in the Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> He scored one goal in the next match, in which Manchester City beat <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a> 2–0.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> On 4 May, Agüero was named <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Manchester_City_F.C._season#Awards" title="2011–12 Manchester City F.C. season">Manchester City Player of The Year</a>. His first goal in the 6–1 away win against Norwich also won him the club's Goal of the Season award.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_game_of_the_season">Final game of the season</span></h5>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:30%; ;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1012376600">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"In my career so far it's the most important goal. You score the goal in the last minute to win the title. You're not sure if that's ever going to happen in your career again. I wish I could tell you how I did it but I can't. I thought for all the world that <a href="/wiki/Mario_Balotelli" title="Mario Balotelli">Mario</a> [Balotelli] was going to have a go himself but he just moved it on one more and it fell at my feet and I just thought: 'Hit the target, hit it as hard as you can and hit the target.' And it went in."</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style=""><small>Sergio Agüero, on his <a href="/wiki/Last-minute_goal" title="Last-minute goal">last-minute goal</a> against Queens Park Rangers in 2012 which won the Premier League for City.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></small></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Five straight wins helped City wipe out the eight-point deficit against United, and they went into the final day's fixtures leading on goal difference. Facing relegation-threatened <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a>, City needed to match or better United's result at <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>. By the 66th minute, QPR's <a href="/wiki/Joey_Barton" title="Joey Barton">Joey Barton</a> was sent off after elbowing Agüero's teammate, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Tevez" title="Carlos Tevez">Carlos Tevez</a> in the face. Eventually after being shown the red card, Barton proceeded to kick Agüero's knee, then attempted to attack <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Kompany" title="Vincent Kompany">Vincent Kompany</a>, only for him to be held back by Micah Richards. Despite that, QPR still went ahead 2–1 against City, while United were 1–0 up against Sunderland. In response, manager Roberto Mancini sent on strikers <a href="/wiki/Edin_D%C5%BEeko" title="Edin Džeko">Edin Džeko</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mario_Balotelli" title="Mario Balotelli">Mario Balotelli</a> in an attempt to get the two goals City now needed for the title. Five minutes of injury time began for City with their and United's match scores still constant. Džeko equalised for City for a glimmer of hope, but United soon finished their own game with a victory. In the 94th minute, Agüero, receiving the ball from Balotelli, drove into the penalty area and placed a powerful low shot into the corner of the goal, clinching the win and the first top flight English title for Manchester City since 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC2012_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2012-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Agüero's goal sent the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Manchester_Stadium" title="City of Manchester Stadium">City of Manchester Stadium</a> into a frenzy and he was dragged to the floor jubilantly by his City teammates. <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Kompany" title="Vincent Kompany">Vincent Kompany</a> recalled that Agüero was crying on the floor,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and when asked if he cried during the Manchester City parade the following day, Agüero stated: "Yeah, a little".<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2012.E2.80.9313_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–13_season"><a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Manchester_City_F.C._season" title="2012–13 Manchester City F.C. season">2012–13 season</a></span></h4>
<p>Agüero started the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_in_English_football" title="2012–13 in English football">2012–13</a> season in the <a href="/wiki/2012_FA_Community_Shield" title="2012 FA Community Shield">2012 FA Community Shield</a> against Chelsea at <a href="/wiki/Villa_Park" title="Villa Park">Villa Park</a> as Manchester City won 3–2.<sup id="cite_ref-2012CommunityShield_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012CommunityShield-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In Manchester City's first league match, Agüero had to be stretchered off in the 13th minute of their home game against <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> due to a knee injury.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Agüero was an unused substitute in City's 3–2 defeat to Real Madrid on 18 September 2012. Following the match, Agüero said he would have joined Real Madrid had they made an offer for him in 2011 but was left with "no option but to join City".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Agüero made his return in a 1–1 home draw against Arsenal in the Premier League and went on to score his first goal of the season against Fulham on 29 September in a 2–1 away win in the Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> He followed this up with another goal the following weekend against Sunderland in a 3–0 home win.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> His next league goal came in a 2–1 win at home against Tottenham on 11 November.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> He followed this up with another two goals the following weekend against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> in a 5–0 win at home.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Agüero also scored in back-to-back games in the Champions League in successive draws at home to <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> and Real Madrid.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> He scored his next goal on 15 December, where he scored the opening goal, as Manchester City won 3–1 away against Newcastle.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Agüero then scored against Norwich City on 29 December in a 4–3 away win.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In his next match on 2 January, after scoring a penalty in the 73rd minute, Agüero damaged his hamstring during a 3–0 victory over Stoke.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Agüero made his return for Manchester City on 19 January after coming on as an 81st-minute substitute in a 2–0 victory against Fulham.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> On 3 February, Agüero scored the equaliser after beating Liverpool goalkeeper Pepe Reina in a race to the ball out near the right corner flag.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> On 17 February, Agüero helped Manchester City to the quarter-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_FA_Cup" title="2012–13 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> as he scored twice in a 4–0 win at home to <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> He sustained a knee injury in the 2–0 win over Chelsea on 24 February.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> This eventually led to him missing the Argentina squad for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(CONMEBOL)" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification (CONMEBOL)">2014 FIFA World Cup qualification</a> matches against <a href="/wiki/Venezuela_national_football_team" title="Venezuela national football team">Venezuela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bolivia_national_football_team" title="Bolivia national football team">Bolivia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Agüero made his return for Manchester City on 30 March after coming on as a substitute with warm reception in a 4–0 victory against Newcastle.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 8 April, Agüero scored a solo goal to give City the win in the Manchester derby in the 78th minute, seven minutes after coming on as a <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitute</a> for <a href="/wiki/Samir_Nasri" title="Samir Nasri">Samir Nasri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Agüero then scored a header to help Manchester City defeat Chelsea on 14 April in the FA Cup semi-final and reach the final.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In the 82nd-minute of the tie, Agüero made a two-footed tackle on <a href="/wiki/David_Luiz" title="David Luiz">David Luiz</a> after the defender had previously appeared to tackle him.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Despite the incident warranting a red card at the time, the FA announced Agüero would not be punished following confirmation that referee <a href="/wiki/Chris_Foy_(referee)" title="Chris Foy (referee)">Chris Foy</a> had at least seen part of the incident and acted on it during the match. Many people disagreed with this decision and felt that the FA had failed to act.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> On 17 April, Agüero revealed that he had apologised to David Luiz for his rash challenge on the defender.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Agüero withdrew as a precaution at half-time on 17 April in Manchester City's 1–0 home victory over Wigan after feeling tightness in a hamstring, but he appeared as an unused substitute in City's 3–1 away loss at <a href="/wiki/White_Hart_Lane" title="White Hart Lane">White Hart Lane</a> against Tottenham on 21 April.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> He scored his next goal on 27 April, where he scored the opening goal, as Manchester City won 2–1 home against <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> On 11 May, Agüero started for Manchester City in the <a href="/wiki/2013_FA_Cup_Final" title="2013 FA Cup Final">2013 FA Cup Final</a>, where the team lost 1–0 to Wigan. Agüero scored his final goal of the season in a 2–0 away win against <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a> on 14 May.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> reported that he was the main transfer target of Spanish giants Real Madrid,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> but Agüero responded by saying, "I'm very happy at City and I feel appreciated and loved here which means a lot to me."<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Manchester City chief executive Ferran Soriano also negated the idea of a transfer, insisting Agüero would stay at the City of Manchester Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> However, former Argentina international <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">Diego Maradona</a> backed him to join Real Madrid, believing Agüero's presence in the Madrid team could help get even more out of <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On 25 May 2013, Agüero signed a one-year extension to his contract, keeping him at Manchester City until 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Agüero stated his commitment to Manchester City on 28 May 2013, saying, "I'm committed to Manchester City, it's a great club."<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2013.E2.80.9314_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–14_season"><a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Manchester_City_F.C._season" title="2013–14 Manchester City F.C. season">2013–14 season</a></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dzeko_kickoff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Dzeko_kickoff.jpg/220px-Dzeko_kickoff.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Dzeko_kickoff.jpg/330px-Dzeko_kickoff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Dzeko_kickoff.jpg/440px-Dzeko_kickoff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dzeko_kickoff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Agüero and <a href="/wiki/Edin_D%C5%BEeko" title="Edin Džeko">Edin Džeko</a> about to kick-off against <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> in August 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Following a knee injury that ruled him out of all of the club's pre-season games,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Agüero scored in City's 4–0 victory over Newcastle United in the opening game of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Premier_League" title="2013–14 Premier League">2013–14 Premier League</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> On 22 September 2013, he scored a brace in a 4–1 home win against Manchester United.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 8 November 2013, after scoring five goals in four matches between 5 October and 2 November, Agüero was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> for the first time. During the same period, he had also scored both goals for City in a 2–1 away win against <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PFC CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 November, after scoring his ninth and tenth goals of the league season in a 6–0 win against Tottenham Hotspur, Agüero overtook <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a> as the player with the highest goals-per-minute ratio in Premier League history.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> He also scored six goals in five matches in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League group stage">Champions League group stage</a> as Manchester City qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_phase" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League knockout phase">knockout phase</a> for the first time.
</p><p>On 14 December 2013, Agüero was substituted in a 6–3 win against Arsenal due to a calf injury<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> and missed eight matches.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> On 16 January 2014, he returned from injury in an <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_FA_Cup" title="2013–14 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> third-round replay against Blackburn Rovers, scoring after coming on as a substitute in the 5–0 win.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> In the next round of the competition, he scored his first hat-trick of the season in a 4–2 victory over <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>. On 29 January, he scored his 50th Premier League goal in a 5–1 victory at Tottenham but was substituted with a hamstring injury.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 March 2014, Agüero returned to the Manchester City team for the <a href="/wiki/2014_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2014 Football League Cup Final">2014 Football League Cup Final</a>, where the team beat Sunderland 3–1 at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2014LeagueCupFinal_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014LeagueCupFinal-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In his third appearance since returning from the hamstring problem, Agüero suffered a recurrence of the injury and was withdrawn at half-time in a 2–1 Champions League loss at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Nou" title="Camp Nou">Camp Nou</a> against Barcelona.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> He missed the team's next five Premier League matches, before returning to the starting line-up in a 3–2 loss against Liverpool at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a> on 13 April.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 April 2014, Agüero scored his first goal since January in a 3–1 defeat of West Bromwich Albion at the City of Manchester Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> After scoring his final goal of the season in a 3–2 win over <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> at <a href="/wiki/Goodison_Park" title="Goodison Park">Goodison Park</a> on 3 May, Agüero started for Manchester City against West Ham as the team secured its second Premier League title in three seasons with a 2–0 win.<sup id="cite_ref-McNulty11May2014_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McNulty11May2014-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2014.E2.80.9315_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–15_season"><a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Manchester_City_F.C._season" title="2014–15 Manchester City F.C. season">2014–15 season</a></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CSKA-MC_(12).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/CSKA-MC_%2812%29.jpg/170px-CSKA-MC_%2812%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/CSKA-MC_%2812%29.jpg/255px-CSKA-MC_%2812%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d4/CSKA-MC_%2812%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="328" data-file-height="477" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CSKA-MC_(12).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Agüero playing against <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PFC CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a> in October 2014</div></div></div>
<p>On 14 August 2014, Agüero signed a new five-year contract to keep him at Manchester City until 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Agüero scored his first goal of <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Manchester_City_F.C._season" title="2014–15 Manchester City F.C. season">2014–15</a> while appearing as an 83rd-minute substitute for Edin Džeko in City's opening match of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Premier_League" title="2014–15 Premier League">Premier League</a> season against Newcastle on 17 August.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Due to his late return from the World Cup, Agüero was again used as a substitute in the second game of the season against Liverpool, but, after replacing Džeko, took just 23 seconds to score City's third goal in the 3–1 win.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 October 2014, he scored all four of City's goals in a 4–1 home win over Tottenham, two of which were penalties; he took another penalty in the match, but it was saved by <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Lloris" title="Hugo Lloris">Hugo Lloris</a>. This took Agüero to 61 Premier League goals for the club, surpassing Carlos Tevez as the club's record scorer in the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> He was the first player in the season to reach ten Premier League goals, doing so with the only goal in the Manchester derby on 2 November.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:33%; ;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1012376600"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">Aguero is every bit as important to them as <a href="/wiki/Luis_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Luis Suárez">Luis Suárez</a> was to Liverpool last year or <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Bale" title="Gareth Bale">Gareth Bale</a> to Tottenham Hotspur the year before.</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— English football journalist <a href="/wiki/Martin_Samuel" title="Martin Samuel">Martin Samuel</a> after City's win over Bayern Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Agüero scored a <a href="/wiki/List_of_UEFA_Champions_League_hat-tricks" title="List of UEFA Champions League hat-tricks">hat-trick</a> in City's 3–2 win over <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2014–15 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage#Group_E" title="2014–15 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a> on 25 November, starting with a penalty which he won himself.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Five days later, in his 100th Premier League match, he was wrongly booked for <a href="/wiki/Diving_(association_football)" title="Diving (association football)">simulation</a> by referee <a href="/wiki/Mike_Jones_(referee)" title="Mike Jones (referee)">Mike Jones</a> after being fouled by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Fonte" title="José Fonte">José Fonte</a> in the penalty area, although City went on to defeat Southampton 3–0.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 December, Agüero was named the <a href="/wiki/Football_Supporters%27_Federation" title="Football Supporters&#39; Federation">Football Supporters' Federation Player of the Year</a> for 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> He was also awarded <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> for November 2014, a month in which he scored three league goals and assisted two more.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Agüero sustained a knee injury in the second minute of Manchester City's 1–0 win over Everton on 6 December<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> and was unable to appear again for the remainder of 2014. He returned to City's matchday squad for the return fixture with Everton at Goodison Park on 10 January 2015<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> and appeared as a 67th-minute substitute in the 1–1 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> On 11 February, Agüero scored his first two goals of 2015 in a 4–1 win at Stoke City.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> On 21 February 72 seconds into a match against Newcastle United, Agüero scored the fastest penalty kick in the Premier League since 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 12 April, Agüero scored twice in a 4–2 Manchester derby loss to Manchester United at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>. His second goal of the match took him to 100 goals for Manchester City in all competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> On 19 April, he scored his 20th Premier League goal of the season in a 2–0 home win against West Ham United.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> He passed 30 goals for the season with a hat-trick in a 6–0 win over Queens Park Rangers at the City of Manchester Stadium on 9 May, relegating the opponents.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> On 24 May, in Manchester City's final match of the season against Southampton, Agüero scored his 26th league goal of the season, ending 2014–15 with the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.9316_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–16_season"><a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Manchester_City_F.C._season" title="2015–16 Manchester City F.C. season">2015–16 season</a></span></h4>
<p>On 7 August 2015, Agüero announced he would be switching from his number 16 shirt to the number 10 shirt, previously worn by teammate <a href="/wiki/Edin_D%C5%BEeko" title="Edin Džeko">Edin Džeko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Nine days later, he opened the scoring in a 3–0 home victory over reigning champions Chelsea.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During City's 2–0 victory away at Everton on 23 August, Agüero halted the game after noticing that an Everton supporter was in need of emergency treatment. The striker alerted the referee and the other players and made sure that the man received attention from the medics.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> On 30 September, Agüero earned and converted a last-minute penalty to give City a 2–1 win at <a href="/wiki/Borussia_M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="Borussia Mönchengladbach">Borussia Mönchengladbach</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2015–16 UEFA Champions League group stage">Champions League group stage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 3 October, Agüero scored five goals against Newcastle in a 6–1 comeback win, joining <a href="/wiki/Andy_Cole" title="Andy Cole">Andy Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jermain_Defoe" title="Jermain Defoe">Jermain Defoe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dimitar_Berbatov" title="Dimitar Berbatov">Dimitar Berbatov</a> in scoring as many in a Premier League game.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> His five goals within 23 minutes of game time made it the fastest five-goal haul since the Premier League started in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Four minutes after scoring his fifth goal in the 62nd minute, Agüero was substituted by manager <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Pellegrini" title="Manuel Pellegrini">Manuel Pellegrini</a>, as he had been receiving treatment due to a leg injury at half time.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 8 October, in a <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(CONMEBOL)" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification (CONMEBOL)">2018 World Cup qualifying match</a> against <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_national_football_team" title="Ecuador national football team">Ecuador</a>, Agüero sustained a hamstring injury early on and was carried off the pitch in tears. Agüero himself said he expected to be out for around four weeks (in which the derby against Manchester United was to be played), although several media outlets later claimed the injury would last for eight weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> He returned on 21 November, scoring in a 1–4 home loss to Liverpool; this was his 85th Premier League goal, making him the top-scoring South American of all time in the division, ahead of his compatriot and former strike partner Carlos Tevez.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 April 2016, Agüero scored a hat-trick in a 3–0 win at Chelsea, ending with a penalty kick. He became the third visiting player to score a Premier League hat-trick at Stamford Bridge, and the fifth player to have three 20-goal seasons in the division.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, he scored his <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_players_with_100_or_more_goals" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Premier League players with 100 or more goals">100th Premier League</a> goal in a 1–1 draw at Newcastle. He reached the century in 147 games, second only to <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a> who did so in 124.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> The goal was also Agüero's sixth against Newcastle for the season, making his just the sixth player in the Premier League era to have scored six goals against the same club in a single campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Agüero ended the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Premier_League" title="2015–16 Premier League">2015–16 Premier League</a> season with 24 goals, one behind Golden Boot winner <a href="/wiki/Harry_Kane" title="Harry Kane">Harry Kane</a> and level with <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Vardy" title="Jamie Vardy">Jamie Vardy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> However, with his goals coming from 30 appearances, Agüero recorded the league's best goals to minute ratio.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.9317_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–17_season"><a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Manchester_City_F.C._season" title="2016–17 Manchester City F.C. season">2016–17 season</a></span></h4>
<p>On 13 August 2016, Agüero scored Manchester City's first competitive goal under the management of <a href="/wiki/Pep_Guardiola" title="Pep Guardiola">Pep Guardiola</a> in a 2–1 victory against Sunderland on the opening day of the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League" title="2016–17 Premier League">2016–17 Premier League</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a league match against West Ham on 28 August, Agüero struck opponent <a href="/wiki/Winston_Reid" title="Winston Reid">Winston Reid</a> in the throat with his arm, an incident which went unpunished by the referee. Reid lost his voice with the strike, and had to be substituted. The FA gave Agüero a three-match ban for violent conduct, accusing him of behaving in an "aggressive manner that was excessive in force and brutal".<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 November 2016, Agüero scored his 150th goal for Manchester City in a 1–1 draw against <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> in the league.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Agüero was sent off in a 1–3 loss to Chelsea on 3 December for a tackle on <a href="/wiki/David_Luiz" title="David Luiz">David Luiz</a> and was given a four-match suspension.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:35%; ;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1012376600"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"He's a legend, and it's a part of history in the club. Aguero's numbers speak for themselves – he is amazing."</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester City">Manchester City</a> Manager <a href="/wiki/Pep_Guardiola" title="Pep Guardiola">Pep Guardiola</a> on Agüero after he scored a hat-trick against <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>, putting him two goals away from becoming club record scorer.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–18_season"><a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Manchester_City_F.C._season" title="2017–18 Manchester City F.C. season">2017–18 season</a></span></h4>
<p>Having scored on Manchester City's opening fixture of the season against <a href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion_F.C." title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion F.C.">Brighton &amp; Hove Albion</a> on 12 August,<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Agüero scored his second goal of the season against Liverpool in a 5–0 win on 9 September. This was his 124th Premier League goal, and saw him overtake Trinidadian <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Yorke" title="Dwight Yorke">Dwight Yorke</a> as the top-scoring non-European in the competition's history.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> One week later, Agüero scored his sixth Premier League hat-trick in a 6–0 win at <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> to put Manchester City top of the league. On 28 September, Agüero was involved in a road accident after attending a <a href="/wiki/Maluma_(singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maluma (singer)">Maluma</a> concert in Amsterdam, when his taxi crashed into a lamppost. He was left with a fractured rib and ruled out for two weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 October, Agüero scored his 177th goal for Manchester City in a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a>, equalling the record set by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Brook" title="Eric Brook">Eric Brook</a>. This was also the <i>Citizens</i> 11th straight win, equalling another club record.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> He scored his record 178th goal for the team on 1 November away at <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a> in a Champions League group game, a 4–2 win that sent his team through to the knockout stages of the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 January, Agüero scored his second hat-trick of the season against Newcastle in a 3–1 win, his second goal being the landmark 350th goal of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> He was later awarded the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> for January, claiming the award for the fifth time in his career.<sup id="cite_ref-PotmJanuary2018_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PotmJanuary2018-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 February, Agüero scored four goals in a 5–1 <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> home thrashing of <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a>, claiming his third hat-trick of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> He opened the scoring in the <a href="/wiki/2018_EFL_Cup_Final" title="2018 EFL Cup Final">2018 EFL Cup Final</a> on 25 February, by chipping <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>'s <a href="/wiki/David_Ospina" title="David Ospina">David Ospina</a> in a 1vs1 situation, ultimately helping City secure a convincing 3–0 victory at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2018EFLCupFinal_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018EFLCupFinal-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2018.E2.80.9319_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–19_season"><a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Manchester_City_F.C._season" title="2018–19 Manchester City F.C. season">2018–19 season</a></span></h4>
